خيار له ولو أقر البائع بالشرط لما قدمناه عن قاضيخان في شرح اشتراط الخبز والكتابة قبيل باب خيار الرؤية، وإلا فالقول للبائع لأن الاختلاف في اشتراط وصف كالاختلاف في اشتراط الخبز ولذا صورها في الفتح بما إذا اشترياه ليلاً لإخراج ما إذا كان نهاراً بمرأى من عينه وقد صارت حادثة الفتوى وأجبت بما ذكرناه والله الموفق للصواب.
Chapter of Invalid Sale. It is built upon the principle we mentioned in Nikah from Muhammad: when indication and naming are combined, then if they differ in genus, the contract is attached to the named and becomes void due to its non-existence; if they are of the same genus, it is attached to the indicated object and valid due to its existence, and the buyer has an option due to the loss of the attribute, like one who buys a slave on the condition that he is a baker but finds him a writer. In our issue, male and female of humans are two genera due to the difference in purposes, and in animals they are one genus due to similarity; this is what is considered, not the origin, like vinegar and dates syrup are two genera, and Wadhari and Zandiji are two genera despite their origin being the same; so stated in al-Hidayah. The mentioned principle from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, is agreed upon here and applies to all other contracts of marriage, hire, reconciliation for intentional killing, khul', emancipation for money, and sale. In the issue of the book, it is void due to the non-existence of the sold item. Hence it becomes clear that male and female of humans are two genera in fiqh, even if they are one genus in logic, because it is the essential [genus] said of many that differ by an internal distinguishing characteristic; genus in fiqh is what is said of many that do not differ greatly in purpose, so two genera are what differ greatly in purpose without regard to the essential. Wadhari (with fath of waw and kasr and 'ajam of dhal then ra' important) is a relative attribution to Wadar, a village of Samarqand; Zandiji (with zay then nun then dal important then ya' then attribution to Zandana with fath of zay and the final nun and jim added contrary to analogy with its origin); thus mentioned the author of al-Hidayah from the mashayikh. It is said in Fath al-Qadir: Among those that differ in genus is if he sold it as a ruby and it turns out to be glass, the sale is void; if he sold it at night as a red ruby and it appears yellow, it is valid and he has an option, as when he sells a slave as a baker and he is a writer; thus mentioned the author, even though the profession of writing is more honorable than baking, and the author was among those who do not differentiate among the mashayikh between the attribute that appears being better than the attribute first designated in establishing the option, as al-Muhit states the option absolutely. Others, including Sadr al-Islam and Zahir al-Din, held that it is only established if the found attribute is inferior. The first was preferred due to loss of the buyer's purpose. The basis of those who differentiated is the earlier case of one who buys a slave on condition that he is a disbeliever but finds him Muslim: no option because it is better than what was designated. It is distinguished by the fact that the purpose (using the slave for what is not suitable) does not differ between Muslim and disbeliever in agriculture and its matters or trade and its matters, unlike specifying baking or writing, which indicates that his need for which he bought is this attribute. And it has become clear from their statements that if one buys gems and then they dispute—the buyer says 'I stipulated ruby' and the seller denies—if what appears is of a different genus from ruby, they take oath and the sale is rescinded because the dispute is over the genus of the sold item; if what appears is of the same genus but the attribute is lost, then if the sold item was in the sight of the buyer at the time of sale, he has no option even if the seller admits the condition, due to what we previously mentioned from Qadikhan in the explanation of stipulating baking and writing before the chapter of option of sight; otherwise, the seller's word is taken because the dispute is over stipulating an attribute, like the dispute over stipulating baking. Hence in al-Fath he gave the example of buying at night to exclude the case when it is daytime and in his sight. The case has become a fatwa issue, and I answered with what we mentioned. And Allah is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the chapter of invalid sales, specifically the effect of misdescription regarding genus (jins). The author begins by recalling the principle from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani used in Nikah: when both indication (ishara) and naming (tasmiya) are present, and they conflict, the outcome depends on whether the named and indicated belong to the same genus or different genera. If different, the contract attaches to the named item (which does not exist) and becomes void. If same genus, the contract attaches to the indicated item (which exists) and is valid, but the buyer has an option (khiyar) because the promised attribute (e.g., being a baker) is missing. The text then applies this to the distinction between male and female humans: legally they are two separate genera because the purposes differ greatly, whereas in animals they are one genus due to close resemblance. This is a fiqhi definition, not logical. Examples are given: vinegar and dates syrup are two genera; Wadhari and Zandiji (types of dates) are considered two genera despite same origin. The principle is unanimous and applies to various contracts. The passage then delves into a Hanafi internal dispute about whether the option exists when the found attribute is better than the stipulated one. One group (Sadr al-Islam, Zahir al-Din) holds that option only exists if the found attribute is inferior; others (including the author of al-Hidayah and al-Muhit) grant option regardless, based on loss of purpose. The text favors the latter. A further distinction is made: if the bought item was seen at the time of sale and the dispute is over an attribute (not genus), the buyer loses the option if he saw it; otherwise, the seller's word is taken. Practical examples and fatwa are given. The key takeaway: genus differences void the contract, attribute differences give option.

Key Terms
الإشارة (al-ishara): Pointing to the actual object in a sale (e.g., pointing to a specific slave).
التسمية (al-tasmiya): Verbally naming or describing the object (e.g., 'a baker slave').
الجنس (al-jins): In fiqh: a category of objects that do not differ greatly in purpose; if purpose differs greatly, they are different genera.
الخيار (al-khiyar): The buyer's option to confirm or rescind the sale due to missing attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle of ishara and tasmiya, if someone sells a slave described as a baker (khabbaz) but the slave is actually a writer (katib), what is the ruling?
A) The sale is void because the attribute differs
B) The sale is valid but the buyer has no option because writing is better than baking
C) The sale is valid and the buyer has an option to rescind
D) The sale is void because the genus differs

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, the distinction between genus and attribute determines whether a misdescription voids the sale or gives the buyer an option; the relied-upon view grants the option even if the actual attribute is superior.

Seller Buying Back Sold Item for Less Before Payment
Ruling with proof on seller's repurchase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of a seller repurchasing his sold item for less before payment, explain the proof from the hadith of Zayd ibn Arqam, and identify the intra-Hanafi exceptions for the heir and agent.

Core Idea
A seller buying back his sold item for less before payment is prohibited as it creates a usurious surplus.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq by Ibn Nujaym explains the prohibition of a seller repurchasing the same item for a lower price before the original payment is made. The ruling is based on a hadith and a rational argument about debt set-off leading to a surplus. The lesson also covers the nuanced Hanafi positions on exceptions like the seller's heir and agent, showing how the school applies legal reasoning to prevent hidden riba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon: the seller buying back the exact item he sold for a lower price before the price is paid. The ruling is that it is not permissible (invalid, fasid).
The prohibition is absolute, applying to any part of the item and any type of agent.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proofs cited: the hadith of Aisha and Zayd ibn Arqam, and the rational argument of set-off leading to a surplus without consideration.
The hadith threat (invalidation of Hajj and Jihad) indicates a major sin.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proof establishes the ruling. The hadith's severe threat implies the act is haram. The rational argument shows that because the price is not yet in the seller's guarantee, a set-off occurs and he gains a surplus without exchanging value.
This surplus is treated like riba al-fadl.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi differences: Abu Hanifa allows the heir and agent to purchase (as principals), Abu Yusuf prohibits in all cases, Muhammad allows the heir but not the agent.
The text also mentions a condition from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: for the heir's purchase to be valid, he must be of acceptable testimony.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the heir's purchase is valid if he is of upright character; the direct seller's purchase is invalid. This balances the prohibition against practical needs.
Later fatwa works like al-Siraj al-Wahhaj refine this with additional conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وشراء ما باع بالأقل قبل النقد) أي لم يجز شراء البائع ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن فهو مرفوع عطفاً على بيع) لا أنه مجرور عطفاً على المجرورات لأنه لو كان كذلك لصار المعنى لم يجز بيع شراء وهو فاسد وإنما منعنا جوازه استدلالاً بقول عائشة رضي تعالى عنها لتلك المرأة وقد باعت بستمائة بعدما اشترت بثمانمائة بئس ما شريت واشتريت ابلغي زيد بن أرقم أن الله تعالى أبطل حجه وجهاده مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن لم يتب. ولأن الثمن لم يدخل في ضمانه فإذا وصل إليه المبيع وقعت المقاصصة فبقي له فضل بلا عوض بخلاف ما إذا باع بالعرض لأن الفضل إنما يظهر عند المجانسة . أطلق في الشراء فشمل شراءه من كل وجه والشراء من وجه كشراء من لا تجوز شهادته له فإنه لا يجوز أيضاً كشرائه بنفسه خلافاً لهما في غير العبد والمكاتب وأطلق فيما باعه فشمل ما باعه بنفسه أو بوكيله وما باعه أصالة أو وكالة كما شمل الشراء لنفسه ولغيره إذا كان هو البائع، وشمل أيضاً شراء الكل أو البعض كما في القنية. وخرج شراء وارث البائع ووكيله عند الإمام لأن العقد وقع له لكونه أصيلاً في الحقوق خلافاً لهما لكونه قائماً مقامه ولكن لا تطيب له الزيادة عند الإمام وإن ملكها، وأما شراء البائع ممن اشترى من مشتريه فجائز وفاقاً. وشرط في السراج الوهاج لجواز شراء وارث البائع أن يكون ممن تجوز شهادته للمورث في حياته وإلا لا يجوز وهو قيد حسن أغفله كثير وإن كان معلوماً من بيان حكم شراء من لا تجوز شهادته له وأراد قوله : (قبل نقد الثمن) قال الرملي وسواء كان الثمن حالاً أو مؤجلاً كما صرح به في الهداية. قوله : (وخرج شراء وارث البائع ووكيله (الخ قال الرملي :م: أبو حنيفة ولم يجعل الموكل مشترياً بشراء الوكيل حتى قال لو باع الرجل شيئاً بنفسه ثم وكل رجلاً أن يشتري له ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن فاشتراه الوكيل فإنه يجوز عنده خلافاً لهما، وكذلك الجواب فيما إذا اشترى من وارث من باع منه بمنزلة الشراء ممن باع ولم يجعل محمد شراء وارث البائع بمنزلة شراء البائع حتى قال : لو مات البائع فاشترى وارثه ما باع بأقل مما باع جاز. وعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا يجوز في الفصلين جميعاً وبعض مشايخنا قالوا: قول أبي يوسف فيما إذا كان المشتري وارثاً للبائع نظير قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله إذا كان غير وارث تقبل شهادته له، إذا كان وارثاً لا تقبل شهادته له كالوالد والولد ومن بمثابتهما لا يجوز شراؤه عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله خلافاً لهما. وبعضهم قالوا : على قول أبي حنيفة يجوز شراء وارث البائع على كل حال سواء كان وارث البائع ممن تقبل شهادته له
His statement: (And buying what he sold for less before payment) means: it is not permissible for the seller to buy what he sold for less than what he sold for before the payment of the price. It is raised as a conjunction to 'sale', not as a genitive conjunction to the genitive items, because if it were such, the meaning would become 'it is not permissible to sell a purchase' which is invalid. We prohibit its permissibility based on the statement of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, to that woman who had sold for six hundred after buying for eight hundred: 'How bad is what you sold and bought!' Convey to Zaid ibn Arqam that Allah has invalidated his Hajj and Jihad with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, if he does not repent. And because the price has not entered into his guarantee, so when the sold item reaches him, a set-off occurs, leaving him with a surplus without consideration, unlike when he sells for a commodity because the surplus only appears when [the items] are homogeneous. He made it absolute regarding purchase, so it includes his purchase from every aspect, and purchase from one aspect like buying from one whose testimony is not acceptable for him; it is also impermissible, like his own purchase, contrary to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in other than a slave and a mukatab. He made it absolute regarding what he sold, so it includes what he sold himself or through his agent, and what he sold as principal or as agent, and also includes purchase for himself and for another if he is the seller, and also includes purchase of the whole or part, as in al-Qunyah. And the purchase of the seller's heir and agent is excluded according to Imam because the contract was concluded for him (the heir/agent) as he is a principal in rights, contrary to them (the two) because he stands in his place; but the increase is not lawful for him according to Imam even if he owns it. As for the seller buying from the one who bought from his buyer, it is permissible by agreement. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, it is conditioned for the validity of the heir's purchase that he be among those whose testimony is acceptable for the testator during his life; otherwise, it is not permissible. This is a good qualification, overlooked by many, even if it is known from the clarification of the ruling on purchasing from one whose testimony is not acceptable. He intended: His statement: (before payment of the price). Al-Ramli said: Whether the price is immediate or deferred, as stated in al-Hidayah. His statement: (And the purchase of the seller's heir and agent is excluded) etc. Al-Ramli said: Abu Hanifa did not make the principal a buyer by the agent's purchase, so he said: if a man sells something himself, then appoints a man to buy for him what he sold for less before payment, and the agent buys it, it is permissible according to him, contrary to them (the two). And similarly, the answer regarding when one buys from the heir of the seller: it is like buying from the seller, and Muhammad did not treat the heir's purchase like the seller's purchase, so he said: if the seller dies and his heir buys what he sold for less, it is permissible. From Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, that it is impermissible in both cases. Some of our mashayikh said: Abu Yusuf's statement regarding when the buyer is an heir to the seller is analogous to Abu Hanifa's statement when a non-heir whose testimony is acceptable for him [buys], but when an heir whose testimony is not acceptable for him like father and son and the like, his purchase is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them (the two). And some said: According to Abu Hanifa, the heir's purchase is permissible in any case, whether the heir is one whose testimony is acceptable for him or not.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on a seller repurchasing the same item he sold for a lower price before the original price is paid. The author clarifies that this is prohibited as it leads to a usurious surplus (faḍl). The proof is from the hadith of Aisha and Zayd ibn Arqam. The reason: the price is not yet in the seller's guarantee, so if he buys back at a lower price, he gets a surplus without consideration. The ruling is absolute: it applies whether the purchase is direct or indirect, and to any part of the sold item. Exceptions: the seller's heir and agent are excluded according to Abu Hanifa, because the contract is considered for them personally, not for the seller. However, the increase is not lawful for them ethically. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ: Abu Yusuf prohibits in both cases, Muhammad allows the heir's purchase. The text also notes a condition from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: for the heir's purchase to be valid, he must be someone whose testimony would have been acceptable for the testator (i.e., not a disqualified witness). The key takeaway: the prohibition is designed to prevent hidden riba, and the school has nuanced positions on proxies.

Key Terms
شراء ما باع بالأقل (shira' ma ba'a bi-l-aqall): The seller buying back the exact item he sold for a lower price before the original price is paid.
المقاصصة (al-muqasassa): Set-off of debts: the buyer owes the price, the seller owes the item; a set-off would create a surplus without consideration.
الفضل (al-fadl): The surplus amount the seller obtains by buying back at a lower price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a seller dies and his heir buys back the sold item for less before the price is paid, what is Abu Hanifa's position?
A) It is invalid because the heir stands in the seller's place
B) It is valid because the heir is a principal, not a representative
C) It is valid only if the heir is a disqualified witness
D) It is invalid according to all Hanafi imams

Key Takeaway
The prohibition prevents a disguised form of riba; exceptions are strictly limited to those who act as principals, not representatives.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling: Seller Cannot Buy Back for Less Before Payment
Commentary on the ruling and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a seller buying back his sold item for less before payment is a corrupt (fasid) sale, and explain the two proofs: the hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam and the legal reasoning of profit without liability (ribh ma lam yadman).

Core Idea
A seller gains profit without liability when repurchasing for less before payment — this is the root of the prohibition.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq states a short rule: the seller cannot buy back what he sold for less before the price is paid. The commentator expands with two proofs — a hadith and a legal principle. In this lesson, we unpack the ruling and its evidence so you can see why the Hanafi school treats this as a corrupt (fasid) transaction, not void (batil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the seller repurchasing the item he sold, for a price lower than the original, before he has paid the full price. The ruling according to the Hanafi school is that it is fasid (corrupt) — not permissible and must be undone.
2
Locate the first proof: the hadith
The commentator cites the hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam: the Prophet threatened nullification of his Hajj and Jihad if he did not repent from such a transaction. This shows the severity of the prohibition.
The hadith is narrated in various collections; it is a single (ahad) hadith with strong indication (dalala qati) of prohibition.
3
Understand the second proof: legal reasoning
The price has not yet entered the seller's guarantee (daman). When the seller gets the item back, he effectively offsets the price he owes, and any difference is a surplus he receives without having taken liability. This is 'profit without liability' (ribh ma lam yadman), which is prohibited.
This reasoning is analogous to the rule that one cannot profit from something without bearing risk.
4
Note the distinction from barter (bay' bi al-'arad)
If the original sale was by barter (non-money commodity), the surplus only appears when the items are homogeneous. This is why the prohibition is limited to monetary sales.
The passage says 'unlike the case if he sold by barter because the surplus only appears when there is homogeneity.'
5
Confirm the hukm level: fasid, not batil
The sale is corrupt but not void. It can be rectified by returning the item; the parties must undo it.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes fasid (defective) from batil (void). The distinction matters for legal consequences such as ownership and liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وشراء ما باع بالأقل قبل النقد) أي لم يجز شراء البائع ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن فهو مرفوع عطفاً على بيع لا أنه مجرور عطفاً على المجرورات لأنه لو كان كذلك لصار المعنى لم يجز بيع شراء وهو فاسد وإنما منعنا جوازه استدلالاً بقول عائشة رضي تعالى عنها لتلك المرأة وقد باعت بستمائة بعدما اشترت بثمانمائة بئس ما شريت واشتريت ابلغي زيد بن أرقم أن الله تعالى أبطل حجه وجهاده مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن لم يتب. ولأن الثمن لم يدخل في ضمانه فإذا وصل إليه المبيع وقعت المقاصصة فبقي له فضل بلا عوض بخلاف ما إذا باع بالعرض لأن الفضل إنما يظهر عند المجانسة . أطلق في الشراء فشمل شراءه من كل وجه والشراء من وجه كشراء من لا تجوز شهادته له فإنه لا يجوز أيضاً كشرائه بنفسه خلافاً لهما في غير العبد والمكاتب وأطلق فيما باعه فشمل ما باعه بنفسه أو بوكيله وما باعه أصالة أو وكالة كما شمل الشراء لنفسه ولغيره إذا كان هو البائع، وشمل أيضاً شراء الكل أو البعض كما في القنية. وخرج شراء وارث البائع ووكيله عند الإمام لأن العقد وقع له لكونه أصيلاً في الحقوق خلافاً لهما لكونه قائماً مقامه ولكن لا تطيب له الزيادة عند الإمام وإن ملكها، وأما شراء البائع ممن اشترى من مشتريه فجائز وفاقاً. وشرط في السراج الوهاج لجواز شراء وارث البائع أن يكون ممن تجوز شهادته للمورث في حياته وإلا لا يجوز وهو قيد حسن أغفله كثير وإن كان معلوماً من بيان حكم شراء من لا تجوز شهادته له وأراد

قوله : (قبل نقد الثمن) قال الرملي وسواء كان الثمن حالاً أو مؤجلاً كما صرح به في الهداية. قوله : (وخرج شراء وارث البائع ووكيله (الخ قال الرملي :م: أبو حنيفة ولم يجعل الموكل مشترياً بشراء الوكيل حتى قال لو باع الرجل شيئاً بنفسه ثم وكل رجلاً أن يشتري له ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن فاشتراه الوكيل فإنه يجوز عنده خلافاً لهما، وكذلك الجواب فيما إذا اشترى من وارث من باع منه بمنزلة الشراء ممن باع ولم يجعل محمد شراء وارث البائع بمنزلة شراء البائع حتى قال : لو مات البائع فاشترى وارثه ما باع بأقل مما باع جاز. وعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا يجوز في الفصلين جميعاً وبعض مشايخنا قالوا: قول أبي يوسف فيما إذا كان المشتري وارثاً للبائع نظير قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله إذا كان غير وارث تقبل شهادته له، إذا كان وارثاً لا تقبل شهادته له كالوالد والولد ومن بمثابتهما لا يجوز شراؤه عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله خلافاً لهما. وبعضهم قالوا : على قول أبي حنيفة يجوز شراء وارث البائع على كل حال سواء كان وارث البائع ممن تقبل شهادته له

المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى الشراء من مشتريه حقيقة أو حكماً كالشراء من وارث مشتريه . والفرق بين الوارثين أن وارث البائع إنما لم يقم مقامه لأن هذا مما لا يورث وهو إنما يقوم مقامه فيما يورث بخلاف وارث المشتري فإنه قام مقامه في ملك العين وهذا من أحكامها. وقيد بما باع لأن المبيع لو انتقص خرج أن يكون شراء ما باع فيكون النقصان من الثمن في مقابلة ما نقص من العين سواء كان النقصان من الثمن بقدر ما نقص منها أو بأكثر منه، وعلى هذا ما تفرع . قالوا لو ولدت الجارية عند المشتري ثم اشتراها البائع بأقل إن كانت الولادة نقصتها جاز كما لو دخلها عيب عند المشتري ثم اشتراها منه بالأقل، وإن لم تنقصها لا يجوز لأنه يحصل به ربح لم يدخل في ضمانه ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولا بد أن يكون النقصان فيها من حيث الذات لأن العين لو نقصت قيمتها بتغير الأسعار لم يجز الشراء بالأقل لأن تغيير السعر غير معتبر في حق الأحكام لأنه فتور في الرغبات لا فوات جزء كما في حق الغاصب وغيره فعاد إليه كما خرج عن ملكه فظهر الربح وقيد بالأقل احترازاً عن المثل أو الأكثر فإنه جائز، ولا بد من اتحاد جنس الثمنين لأنه حينئذ يظهر النقصان فإن اختلف الجنس جاز مطلقاً والدراهم والدنانير هنا جنس واحد احتياطاً، وقدمنا أنهما جنسان إلا في ثمانية في أول البيوع فإذا كان النقد الثاني أقل من قيمة الأول لم يجز وأطلق في الأقلية فشمل الأقل قدراً والأقل وصفاً، فلو باع بألف نسيئة إلى سنة ثم اشتراه بألف نسيئة إلى سنتين فسد عندنا. وقيد بقوله «قبل النقد» إذ بعده لا فساد وفي القنية لو قبض نصف الثمن ثم اشترى النصف بأقل من نصف الثمن لم يجز وكذا لو أحال البائع على المشتري اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : لا يجوز أن يشتريه بأقل من الثمن وإن بقي من ثمنه درهم، ولا بد من نقد جميع الثمن، ولو خرج المبيع عن ملك المشتري ثم عاد إليه فإن عاد إليه بحكم ملك جديد كالإقالة قبل القبض أو بعده أو بالشراء أو الهبة أو بالميراث فشراء البائع منه بالأقل جائز، وإن عاد إليه بما هو فسخ بخيار رؤية أو شرط قبل القبض أو بعده فالشراء منه بالأقل لا يجوز؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وذكر الشارح هنا فروعاً فقال (۱) .
قوله: (وصح فيما ضم إليه) أي صح البيع في المضموم إلى شراء ما باعه بالأقل قبل النقد كأن اشترى جارية بخمسمائة ثم باعها وأخرى معها من البائع قبل أن ينقده الثمن بخمسمائه فالبيع جائز في التي لم يشترها من البائع ويفسد في الأخرى لأنه لا بد أن يجعل
أو لا كما هو قول محمد رحمه الله وتمامه في التتارخانية. قوله : (خلافاً لهما) أي في مسألة شراء الوكيل كما يفيده التعليل وعبارة التتارخانية السابقة. قوله : (إن) وارث البائع إنما لم يقم مقامه الخ) هذا وجه ما قدمه آنفاً عن السراج واستحسنه . (۱) بياض بالأصل.
انظر مع
His statement: (And the purchase of what he sold for less before payment) means it is not permissible for the seller to buy back what he sold for less than what he sold for before paying the price. So it is in the nominative as a conjunction on 'sale', not in the genitive as a conjunction on the genitives, because if it were so the meaning would become 'a sale of purchase is not permissible' and it is corrupt. Rather we prevented its permissibility deducing from the statement of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, to that woman who had sold for six hundred after buying for eight hundred: 'How bad is what you sold and bought. Inform Zaid ibn Arqam that Allah Almighty has nullified his Hajj and Jihad with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, if he does not repent.' And because the price has not entered his guarantee, so when the sold item reaches him, a set-off occurs and a surplus remains for him without compensation, unlike the case if he sold by barter because the surplus only appears when there is homogeneity. He used absolute terms in 'purchase' so it includes his purchase from every aspect, and purchase from one aspect like purchase from one whose testimony is not permissible for him, for it is also not permissible like his own purchase, contrary to the two companions regarding a slave or a mukatab. And he used absolute terms in 'what he sold' so it includes what he sold himself or through his agent, and what he sold as principal or agent, just as it includes the purchase for himself or for another if he is the seller. It also includes purchase of the whole or part as in al-Qunyah. And excluded is the purchase by the seller's heir and agent according to the Imam, because the contract occurred for him as he is the principal in rights, contrary to the two companions because he stands in his place, but the increase is not lawful for him according to the Imam even if he owns it. As for the seller purchasing from someone who bought from his buyer, it is permissible by agreement. And it is stipulated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj for the permissibility of the seller's heir's purchase that he be one whose testimony is accepted for the testator during his life, otherwise it is not permissible, and it is a good condition that many have overlooked, even if it is known from the explanation of the ruling on purchasing from one whose testimony is not accepted for him... His statement: (before payment of the price). Al-Ramli said: It is the same whether the price is immediate or deferred, as explicitly stated in al-Hidayah. His statement: (And excluded is the purchase of the seller's heir and agent etc.) Al-Ramli said: This is the view of Abu Hanifa, and he did not consider the principal as the buyer by the agent's purchase, so that he said: If a man sells something himself, then appoints a man to buy for him what he sold for less than what he sold before payment of the price, and the agent buys it, then it is permissible according to him, contrary to the two companions. And similarly the answer when he purchases from the heir of one who sold to him is like the purchase from the one who sold. And Muhammad did not consider the purchase by the seller's heir as like the purchase by the seller, so that he said: If the seller dies and his heir buys what he sold for less than what he sold, it is permissible. And from Abu Yusuf may Allah have mercy on him that it is not permissible in both cases. Some of our scholars said: The statement of Abu Yusuf when the buyer is an heir of the seller is analogous to the statement of Abu Hanifa when he is not an heir—if his testimony is accepted for him, and if he is an heir, his testimony is not accepted for him, like the father and son and those similar to them, so his purchase is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions. And some said: According to Abu Hanifa, the purchase of the seller's heir is permissible in all cases, whether the seller's heir is one whose testimony is accepted for him or not. The author, may Allah have mercy on him: The purchase from his buyer is either real or virtual, like the purchase from the heir of his buyer. And the difference between the two heirs is that the seller's heir did not stand in his place because this is something that is not inherited, and he only stands in his place in matters that are inherited, unlike the buyer's heir, for he stands in his place in ownership of the item and this is among its rulings. And he restricted it to 'what he sold' because if the sold item has decreased, it would not be 'buying what he sold', so the decrease in price corresponds to the decrease in the item, whether the decrease in price is equal to the decrease in the item or more. And on this depend the branches. They said: If the slave girl gives birth while with the buyer, then the seller buys her for less: if the birth decreased her, it is permissible, just as if a defect occurred in her while with the buyer and he bought her from him for less; if it did not decrease her, it is not permissible because it results in profit that did not enter his guarantee. So in Fath al-Qadir. And the decrease must be in the essence, because if the value of the item decreased due to price fluctuation, it is not permissible to buy for less because change in price is not considered in rulings, as it is a slackening of desires, not a loss of a part, as in the case of a usurper and others. So it returned to him as it left his ownership, and profit appears. And he restricted it to 'less' to exclude the equal or more, for it is permissible. And there must be unity of the type of the two prices, because then the decrease appears; if the types differ, it is permissible absolutely. And dirhams and dinars here are one type as a precaution, though we previously stated they are two types except in eight cases at the beginning of the book of sales. So if the second payment is less in value than the first, it is not permissible. And he used absolute terms in 'less', so it includes less in amount and less in description. Thus if he sold for one thousand deferred for one year, then bought it for one thousand deferred for two years, it is corrupt according to us. And he restricted it by his statement 'before payment', because after it there is no corruption. And in al-Qunyah: If he received half of the price, then bought half for less than half of the price, it is not permissible. Similarly, if the seller assigned the price to the buyer. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: It is not permissible for him to buy it for less than the price even if only one dirham remains of its price, and all of the price must be paid. And if the sold item leaves the ownership of the buyer and then returns to him: if it returns to him by a new ownership, like cancellation before or after possession, or by purchase, gift, or inheritance, then the seller's purchase from him for less is permissible; if it returns to him by way of rescission due to option of sight or condition before or after possession, then the purchase from him for less is not permissible. So in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. And the commentator mentioned here branches, saying (1). His statement: (And it is valid in what is joined to it) means the sale is valid in the item joined to the purchase of what he sold for less before payment, such as if he bought a slave girl for five hundred, then sold her and another with her to the seller before paying the price for five hundred: the sale is valid for the one he did not buy from the seller, and corrupt for the other, because it is necessary to make... or not, as is the statement of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, and its completion is in al-Tatar Khaniyya. His statement: (contrary to the two companions) refers to the issue of the agent's purchase, as indicated by the reasoning and the expression of al-Tatar Khaniyya previously. His statement: (That the seller's heir did not stand in his place etc.) is the face of what he previously presented from al-Siraj and approved it. (1) Blank in the original. See with...
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, specifically on the ruling that a seller cannot buy back an item he sold for less than the original sale price before that price has been fully paid. The commentator begins by explaining the grammar of the phrase to confirm the correct meaning: it is a prohibition of the seller's repurchase at a lower price. He then provides two proofs: the hadith of the woman who bought at eight hundred and sold at six hundred, and the more specific hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam where the Prophet threatened nullification of his Hajj and Jihad unless he repented of a similar transaction. The legal reasoning is that since the price was not yet guaranteed (the seller had not taken liability for the price), any surplus he gains by repurchasing is profit without liability (ribh ma lam yadman). This is the basis of the prohibition.

The commentary then expands on the conditions and scope of the ruling. 'Purchase' is absolute, including direct purchase, purchase through an agent, and purchase from one whose testimony is not acceptable. However, the purchase by the seller's heir and agent is excluded according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the contract was originally for the seller himself, and the heir does not stand in his place for this particular ruling (as it is not inherited). This leads to a dispute with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf prohibits both, Muhammad permits the heir's purchase. The commentary also discusses the condition of 'before payment' – the prohibition only applies while the full price remains unpaid; even partial payment or assignment of the price does not lift it. The price can be immediate or deferred; the prohibition remains until full payment.

Further details are explained: the decrease in the item's value (if it occurs at the buyer's hand) allows a lower price without corruption, but only if the decrease is in the essence (such as a defect or birth of a child that reduces value), not simply market fluctuation. The two prices must be of the same type to show the decrease; if different types are used, the purchase is permissible. The term 'less' includes less in amount and less in description (e.g., a longer deferment period). If the item returns to the buyer by a new ownership (cancellation, new purchase, gift, inheritance), the seller's repurchase for less is valid; but if it returns by rescission (option of sight or condition), it is not valid. Finally, if the seller repurchases the item together with another item in a single transaction, the sale is valid for the additional item but corrupt for the original.

Key Terms
شراء ما باع بالأقل قبل النقد (shira' ma ba'a bil-aqal qabl al-naqd): The act of the seller buying back the item he previously sold for a lower price than the original sale price before the original price has been fully paid.
قبل النقد (qabl al-naqd): Before the payment of the price; the prohibition applies as long as the full price remains unpaid, whether the price was immediate or deferred.
وارث البائع (warith al-ba'i'): The heir of the seller; the text discusses whether this heir can buy back the item at a lower price, with a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.
فساد (fasad): Corruption (of a sale); the sale is defective and must be rescinded, but it is not void (batil) and may be rectified by returning the item.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what was threatened to Zaid ibn Arqam if he did not repent from this type of transaction?
A) Excommunication from the community
B) Nullification of his Hajj and Jihad
C) A fine of one thousand dirhams
D) Imprisonment

Key Takeaway
The seller cannot buy back at a discount before paying the price because it yields profit without liability.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
Scope and Dispute: Heir, Agent, and Conditions
Commentary on the conditions and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the conditions of the prohibition (e.g., before payment, same price type, decrease in item) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the seller's heir and agent.

Core Idea
The prohibition extends to any purchase at a lower price before full payment, but the seller's heir and agent are disputed — Abu Hanifa says no, Muhammad says yes for the heir.

After establishing the core ruling, the commentator delves into the boundaries of the prohibition: what counts as 'less', what happens if the item decreases, and whether the seller's heir or agent can make the purchase. Here we will sort out these conditions and the famous disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scope of 'before payment'
The prohibition applies as long as any part of the price remains unpaid; even a single dirham. The price can be immediate or deferred.
Al-Ramli confirms both cases.
2
Analyze the condition of 'less'
Less includes less in amount and less in description (e.g., a longer payment term). The two prices must be of the same type to show the decrease. If types differ (e.g., dirhams vs. dinars), the purchase is allowed because the decrease is not apparent.
Dirhams and dinars are considered one type here as a precaution.
3
Examine the exception for decrease in the item
If the item itself decreased in value due to a defect or birth, buying back for less is allowed. This is not profit without liability because the decrease corresponds to a loss in the item.
Market price fluctuation is not considered a decrease in the item itself.
4
Understand the dispute over the seller's heir and agent
Abu Hanifa: the heir and agent cannot buy back for less because the contract was for the seller. The heir does not inherit the 'right to repurchase'. Abu Yusuf prohibits both, while Muhammad permits the heir but not the agent.
The text provides a detailed reasoning why the heir does not stand in the seller's place.
5
Note the effect of returning the item to the buyer
If the item returns to the buyer by a new ownership (e.g., cancellation, gift), the seller's repurchase is valid. If by rescission (e.g., option of sight), it is not.
This shows that the prohibition is tied to the original sale relationship.

قوله: (وشراء ما باع بالأقل قبل النقد) أي لم يجز شراء البائع ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن فهو مرفوع عطفاً على بيع لا أنه مجرور عطفاً على المجرورات لأنه لو كان كذلك لصار المعنى لم يجز بيع شراء وهو فاسد وإنما منعنا جوازه استدلالاً بقول عائشة رضي تعالى عنها لتلك المرأة وقد باعت بستمائة بعدما اشترت بثمانمائة بئس ما شريت واشتريت ابلغي زيد بن أرقم أن الله تعالى أبطل حجه وجهاده مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن لم يتب. ولأن الثمن لم يدخل في ضمانه فإذا وصل إليه المبيع وقعت المقاصصة فبقي له فضل بلا عوض بخلاف ما إذا باع بالعرض لأن الفضل إنما يظهر عند المجانسة . أطلق في الشراء فشمل شراءه من كل وجه والشراء من وجه كشراء من لا تجوز شهادته له فإنه لا يجوز أيضاً كشرائه بنفسه خلافاً لهما في غير العبد والمكاتب وأطلق فيما باعه فشمل ما باعه بنفسه أو بوكيله وما باعه أصالة أو وكالة كما شمل الشراء لنفسه ولغيره إذا كان هو البائع، وشمل أيضاً شراء الكل أو البعض كما في القنية. وخرج شراء وارث البائع ووكيله عند الإمام لأن العقد وقع له لكونه أصيلاً في الحقوق خلافاً لهما لكونه قائماً مقامه ولكن لا تطيب له الزيادة عند الإمام وإن ملكها، وأما شراء البائع ممن اشترى من مشتريه فجائز وفاقاً. وشرط في السراج الوهاج لجواز شراء وارث البائع أن يكون ممن تجوز شهادته للمورث في حياته وإلا لا يجوز وهو قيد حسن أغفله كثير وإن كان معلوماً من بيان حكم شراء من لا تجوز شهادته له وأراد

قوله : (قبل نقد الثمن) قال الرملي وسواء كان الثمن حالاً أو مؤجلاً كما صرح به في الهداية. قوله : (وخرج شراء وارث البائع ووكيله (الخ قال الرملي :م: أبو حنيفة ولم يجعل الموكل مشترياً بشراء الوكيل حتى قال لو باع الرجل شيئاً بنفسه ثم وكل رجلاً أن يشتري له ما باع بأقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن فاشتراه الوكيل فإنه يجوز عنده خلافاً لهما، وكذلك الجواب فيما إذا اشترى من وارث من باع منه بمنزلة الشراء ممن باع ولم يجعل محمد شراء وارث البائع بمنزلة شراء البائع حتى قال : لو مات البائع فاشترى وارثه ما باع بأقل مما باع جاز. وعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أنه لا يجوز في الفصلين جميعاً وبعض مشايخنا قالوا: قول أبي يوسف فيما إذا كان المشتري وارثاً للبائع نظير قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله إذا كان غير وارث تقبل شهادته له، إذا كان وارثاً لا تقبل شهادته له كالوالد والولد ومن بمثابتهما لا يجوز شراؤه عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله خلافاً لهما. وبعضهم قالوا : على قول أبي حنيفة يجوز شراء وارث البائع على كل حال سواء كان وارث البائع ممن تقبل شهادته له

المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى الشراء من مشتريه حقيقة أو حكماً كالشراء من وارث مشتريه . والفرق بين الوارثين أن وارث البائع إنما لم يقم مقامه لأن هذا مما لا يورث وهو إنما يقوم مقامه فيما يورث بخلاف وارث المشتري فإنه قام مقامه في ملك العين وهذا من أحكامها. وقيد بما باع لأن المبيع لو انتقص خرج أن يكون شراء ما باع فيكون النقصان من الثمن في مقابلة ما نقص من العين سواء كان النقصان من الثمن بقدر ما نقص منها أو بأكثر منه، وعلى هذا ما تفرع . قالوا لو ولدت الجارية عند المشتري ثم اشتراها البائع بأقل إن كانت الولادة نقصتها جاز كما لو دخلها عيب عند المشتري ثم اشتراها منه بالأقل، وإن لم تنقصها لا يجوز لأنه يحصل به ربح لم يدخل في ضمانه ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ولا بد أن يكون النقصان فيها من حيث الذات لأن العين لو نقصت قيمتها بتغير الأسعار لم يجز الشراء بالأقل لأن تغيير السعر غير معتبر في حق الأحكام لأنه فتور في الرغبات لا فوات جزء كما في حق الغاصب وغيره فعاد إليه كما خرج عن ملكه فظهر الربح وقيد بالأقل احترازاً عن المثل أو الأكثر فإنه جائز، ولا بد من اتحاد جنس الثمنين لأنه حينئذ يظهر النقصان فإن اختلف الجنس جاز مطلقاً والدراهم والدنانير هنا جنس واحد احتياطاً، وقدمنا أنهما جنسان إلا في ثمانية في أول البيوع فإذا كان النقد الثاني أقل من قيمة الأول لم يجز وأطلق في الأقلية فشمل الأقل قدراً والأقل وصفاً، فلو باع بألف نسيئة إلى سنة ثم اشتراه بألف نسيئة إلى سنتين فسد عندنا. وقيد بقوله «قبل النقد» إذ بعده لا فساد وفي القنية لو قبض نصف الثمن ثم اشترى النصف بأقل من نصف الثمن لم يجز وكذا لو أحال البائع على المشتري اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج : لا يجوز أن يشتريه بأقل من الثمن وإن بقي من ثمنه درهم، ولا بد من نقد جميع الثمن، ولو خرج المبيع عن ملك المشتري ثم عاد إليه فإن عاد إليه بحكم ملك جديد كالإقالة قبل القبض أو بعده أو بالشراء أو الهبة أو بالميراث فشراء البائع منه بالأقل جائز، وإن عاد إليه بما هو فسخ بخيار رؤية أو شرط قبل القبض أو بعده فالشراء منه بالأقل لا يجوز؛ كذا في السراج الوهاج. وذكر الشارح هنا فروعاً فقال (۱) .
قوله: (وصح فيما ضم إليه) أي صح البيع في المضموم إلى شراء ما باعه بالأقل قبل النقد كأن اشترى جارية بخمسمائة ثم باعها وأخرى معها من البائع قبل أن ينقده الثمن بخمسمائه فالبيع جائز في التي لم يشترها من البائع ويفسد في الأخرى لأنه لا بد أن يجعل
أو لا كما هو قول محمد رحمه الله وتمامه في التتارخانية. قوله : (خلافاً لهما) أي في مسألة شراء الوكيل كما يفيده التعليل وعبارة التتارخانية السابقة. قوله : (إن) وارث البائع إنما لم يقم مقامه الخ) هذا وجه ما قدمه آنفاً عن السراج واستحسنه . (۱) بياض بالأصل.
انظر مع
His statement: (And the purchase of what he sold for less before payment) means it is not permissible for the seller to buy back what he sold for less than what he sold for before paying the price. So it is in the nominative as a conjunction on 'sale', not in the genitive as a conjunction on the genitives, because if it were so the meaning would become 'a sale of purchase is not permissible' and it is corrupt. Rather we prevented its permissibility deducing from the statement of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, to that woman who had sold for six hundred after buying for eight hundred: 'How bad is what you sold and bought. Inform Zaid ibn Arqam that Allah Almighty has nullified his Hajj and Jihad with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, if he does not repent.' And because the price has not entered his guarantee, so when the sold item reaches him, a set-off occurs and a surplus remains for him without compensation, unlike the case if he sold by barter because the surplus only appears when there is homogeneity. He used absolute terms in 'purchase' so it includes his purchase from every aspect, and purchase from one aspect like purchase from one whose testimony is not permissible for him, for it is also not permissible like his own purchase, contrary to the two companions regarding a slave or a mukatab. And he used absolute terms in 'what he sold' so it includes what he sold himself or through his agent, and what he sold as principal or agent, just as it includes the purchase for himself or for another if he is the seller. It also includes purchase of the whole or part as in al-Qunyah. And excluded is the purchase by the seller's heir and agent according to the Imam, because the contract occurred for him as he is the principal in rights, contrary to the two companions because he stands in his place, but the increase is not lawful for him according to the Imam even if he owns it. As for the seller purchasing from someone who bought from his buyer, it is permissible by agreement. And it is stipulated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj for the permissibility of the seller's heir's purchase that he be one whose testimony is accepted for the testator during his life, otherwise it is not permissible, and it is a good condition that many have overlooked, even if it is known from the explanation of the ruling on purchasing from one whose testimony is not accepted for him... His statement: (before payment of the price). Al-Ramli said: It is the same whether the price is immediate or deferred, as explicitly stated in al-Hidayah. His statement: (And excluded is the purchase of the seller's heir and agent etc.) Al-Ramli said: This is the view of Abu Hanifa, and he did not consider the principal as the buyer by the agent's purchase, so that he said: If a man sells something himself, then appoints a man to buy for him what he sold for less than what he sold before payment of the price, and the agent buys it, then it is permissible according to him, contrary to the two companions. And similarly the answer when he purchases from the heir of one who sold to him is like the purchase from the one who sold. And Muhammad did not consider the purchase by the seller's heir as like the purchase by the seller, so that he said: If the seller dies and his heir buys what he sold for less than what he sold, it is permissible. And from Abu Yusuf may Allah have mercy on him that it is not permissible in both cases. Some of our scholars said: The statement of Abu Yusuf when the buyer is an heir of the seller is analogous to the statement of Abu Hanifa when he is not an heir—if his testimony is accepted for him, and if he is an heir, his testimony is not accepted for him, like the father and son and those similar to them, so his purchase is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions. And some said: According to Abu Hanifa, the purchase of the seller's heir is permissible in all cases, whether the seller's heir is one whose testimony is accepted for him or not. The author, may Allah have mercy on him: The purchase from his buyer is either real or virtual, like the purchase from the heir of his buyer. And the difference between the two heirs is that the seller's heir did not stand in his place because this is something that is not inherited, and he only stands in his place in matters that are inherited, unlike the buyer's heir, for he stands in his place in ownership of the item and this is among its rulings. And he restricted it to 'what he sold' because if the sold item has decreased, it would not be 'buying what he sold', so the decrease in price corresponds to the decrease in the item, whether the decrease in price is equal to the decrease in the item or more. And on this depend the branches. They said: If the slave girl gives birth while with the buyer, then the seller buys her for less: if the birth decreased her, it is permissible, just as if a defect occurred in her while with the buyer and he bought her from him for less; if it did not decrease her, it is not permissible because it results in profit that did not enter his guarantee. So in Fath al-Qadir. And the decrease must be in the essence, because if the value of the item decreased due to price fluctuation, it is not permissible to buy for less because change in price is not considered in rulings, as it is a slackening of desires, not a loss of a part, as in the case of a usurper and others. So it returned to him as it left his ownership, and profit appears. And he restricted it to 'less' to exclude the equal or more, for it is permissible. And there must be unity of the type of the two prices, because then the decrease appears; if the types differ, it is permissible absolutely. And dirhams and dinars here are one type as a precaution, though we previously stated they are two types except in eight cases at the beginning of the book of sales. So if the second payment is less in value than the first, it is not permissible. And he used absolute terms in 'less', so it includes less in amount and less in description. Thus if he sold for one thousand deferred for one year, then bought it for one thousand deferred for two years, it is corrupt according to us. And he restricted it by his statement 'before payment', because after it there is no corruption. And in al-Qunyah: If he received half of the price, then bought half for less than half of the price, it is not permissible. Similarly, if the seller assigned the price to the buyer. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: It is not permissible for him to buy it for less than the price even if only one dirham remains of its price, and all of the price must be paid. And if the sold item leaves the ownership of the buyer and then returns to him: if it returns to him by a new ownership, like cancellation before or after possession, or by purchase, gift, or inheritance, then the seller's purchase from him for less is permissible; if it returns to him by way of rescission due to option of sight or condition before or after possession, then the purchase from him for less is not permissible. Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, specifically on the ruling that a seller cannot buy back an item he sold for less than the original sale price before that price has been fully paid. The commentator begins by explaining the grammar of the phrase to confirm the correct meaning: it is a prohibition of the seller's repurchase at a lower price. He then provides two proofs: the hadith of the woman who bought at eight hundred and sold at six hundred, and the more specific hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam where the Prophet threatened nullification of his Hajj and Jihad unless he repented of a similar transaction. The legal reasoning is that since the price was not yet guaranteed (the seller had not taken liability for the price), any surplus he gains by repurchasing is profit without liability (ribh ma lam yadman). This is the basis of the prohibition.

The commentary then expands on the conditions and scope of the ruling. 'Purchase' is absolute, including direct purchase, purchase through an agent, and purchase from one whose testimony is not acceptable. However, the purchase by the seller's heir and agent is excluded according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because the contract was originally for the seller himself, and the heir does not stand in his place for this particular ruling (as it is not inherited). This leads to a dispute with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf prohibits both, Muhammad permits the heir's purchase. The commentary also discusses the condition of 'before payment' – the prohibition only applies while the full price remains unpaid; even partial payment or assignment of the price does not lift it. The price can be immediate or deferred; the prohibition remains until full payment.

Further details are explained: the decrease in the item's value (if it occurs at the buyer's hand) allows a lower price without corruption, but only if the decrease is in the essence (such as a defect or birth of a child that reduces value), not simply market fluctuation. The two prices must be of the same type to show the decrease; if different types are used, the purchase is permissible. The term 'less' includes less in amount and less in description (e.g., a longer deferment period). If the item returns to the buyer by a new ownership (cancellation, new purchase, gift, inheritance), the seller's repurchase for less is valid; but if it returns by rescission (option of sight or condition), it is not valid. Finally, if the seller repurchases the item together with another item in a single transaction, the sale is valid for the additional item but corrupt for the original.

Key Terms
شراء ما باع بالأقل قبل النقد (shira' ma ba'a bil-aqal qabl al-naqd): The act of the seller buying back the item he previously sold for a lower price than the original sale price before the original price has been fully paid.
قبل النقد (qabl al-naqd): Before the payment of the price; the prohibition applies as long as the full price remains unpaid, whether the price was immediate or deferred.
وارث البائع (warith al-ba'i'): The heir of the seller; the text discusses whether this heir can buy back the item at a lower price, with a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.
فساد (fasad): Corruption (of a sale); the sale is defective and must be rescinded, but it is not void (batil) and may be rectified by returning the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the minimum remaining amount of the original price that still triggers the prohibition?
A) Half of the price
B) A quarter of the price
C) A single dirham
D) The prohibition is lifted once any payment is made

Key Takeaway
The prohibition's scope includes the seller's agents and, according to Abu Hanifa, the seller's heir; but Muhammad permits the heir's purchase, leading to a practical difference in fatwa.

Buying Back Sold Item at Lower Price: Valid Only on Decrease
Explains ruling and exception for seller buying back sold item at lower price.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a seller buying back his sold item at a lower price and apply the exception for decreased value.

Core Idea
A seller cannot buy back his own sold item at a lower price unless the item has decreased in value — profit requires liability.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical issue: after selling an item, can the seller repurchase it from the buyer at a lower price? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the principle of ḍamān (liability). The general rule is that such a buyback is invalid because it yields a profit without bearing risk, but an exception exists when the item has decreased in value while with the buyer. Understanding this exception is essential for correctly applying sales law in everyday transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is the seller buying back the exact same item he sold from the buyer. The general ruling is that it is invalid (fasid) if the price is lower, because the seller profits without having borne the risk of the item during the buyer's ownership.
The key term here is 'buying what he sold' — the item must be unchanged.
2
Locate the dalil: the principle of ḍamān
The proof is rational (qiyas) based on the legal maxim 'al-kharāj bi al-ḍamān' (profit accompanies liability). The seller did not bear any risk after the sale, so any profit from repurchasing at a lower price is unjustified.
This is a central principle in Hanafi sales law.
3
Identify the exception: decrease in the item
If the item has decreased in value while with the buyer (e.g., a defect, birth of a slave girl), then buying back at a lower price is allowed. The decrease justifies the lower price, as the seller is compensating for the loss incurred by the buyer.
The decrease can be physical (like a defect) or legal (like a birth that reduces value).
4
Apply to the example of the slave girl
The passage gives the example: if a slave girl gives birth at the buyer's possession and that birth decreases her market value, the seller may buy her back for less. The lower price corresponds to the decrease, so no unjust profit occurs.
If the birth did not decrease value, the buyback at lower price remains invalid.
5
Consider the practical consequence
The ruling protects both parties: the buyer is compensated for the loss suffered, and the seller does not acquire a windfall. In modern contexts, this applies to any used item whose value drops while in the buyer's hands.
The same principle applies whether the decrease is exactly matched or even exceeded by the price reduction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى الشراء من مشتريه حقيقة أو حكماً كالشراء من وارث مشتريه . والفرق بين الوارثين أن وارث البائع إنما لم يقم مقامه لأن هذا مما لا يورث وهو إنما يقوم مقامه فيما يورث بخلاف وارث المشتري فإنه قام مقامه في ملك العين وهذا من أحكامها. وقيد بما باع لأن المبيع لو انتقص خرج أن يكون شراء ما باع فيكون النقصان من الثمن في مقابلة ما نقص من العين سواء كان النقصان من الثمن بقدر ما نقص منها أو بأكثر منه، وعلى هذا ما تفرع . قالوا لو ولدت الجارية عند المشتري ثم اشتراها البائع بأقل إن كانت الولادة نقصتها جاز كما لو دخلها عيب عند المشتري ثم اشتراها منه بالأقل، وإن لم تنقصها لا يجوز لأنه يحصل به ربح لم يدخل في ضمانه ؛ كذا في فتح القدير.
The author, may Allah have mercy on him, said: The purchase from his buyer is literally or effectively, like buying from the heir of his buyer. The difference between the two heirs is that the heir of the seller does not take his place because this is not inherited, and he only takes his place in what is inherited, unlike the heir of the buyer, for he takes his place in ownership of the 'ayn and this is among its rulings. He restricted it with 'what he sold' because if the sold item had decreased, it would cease to be a purchase of what he sold, so the decrease in the price is in return for what decreased from the 'ayn, whether the decrease in price is equivalent to the decrease in it or more. Based on this are the branches. They said: if the slave girl gives birth while in the possession of the buyer, then the seller buys her for less, if the birth decreased her, it is permitted, just as if a defect entered her while with the buyer and then he bought her from him for less. If it did not decrease her, it is not permitted because it results in profit that was not under his guarantee. This is in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the author of Al-Bahr al-Raiq on the condition when a seller buys back an item he sold. The rule is that if the seller buys back the exact same item from the buyer before the buyer has paid the full price, and he buys it at a lower price, this is not permitted because it results in a profit that the seller obtained without bearing the risk (damān). However, if the item has decreased in value while with the buyer—for example, a slave girl gave birth, which reduces her value, or the item acquired a defect—then buying back at a lower price is allowed, provided the decrease in price corresponds to the decrease in the item. This is based on the principle that profit must be accompanied by liability (al-kharāj bi al-ḍamān).

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for risk and loss; profit without bearing risk is prohibited.
العين (al-ʿayn): The physical item itself, as opposed to its value or benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a seller buys back a slave girl from the buyer at a lower price after she gave birth at the buyer's place, and the birth decreased her value?
A) Invalid
B) Valid if the decrease in price matches the decrease in value
C) Valid only if the seller pays more
D) Valid irrespective of the reason

Key Takeaway
A seller may repurchase his sold item at a lower price only if the item has decreased in value while in the buyer's possession.

Condition for Decrease in Essence and Same Type of Price
States two conditions for valid buyback at lower price with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for buying back a sold item at a lower price and apply them to distinguish between physical decrease and market fluctuation.

Core Idea
A price drop from market fluctuation does not permit buying back at a lower price; only a physical decrease in the item's essence qualifies.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key condition in the law of buyback (al-shira' bi al-aqall). When a seller repurchases an item they previously sold at a lower price, the decrease must be in the item's essence (al-dhat), not its market value. Additionally, the two prices must be of the same currency type. Understanding these conditions prevents using market fluctuations to circumvent riba or create uncertainty in sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Identify the act (buying back a sold item at a lower price) and the two conditions stated: the decrease must be in the essence (dhāt), and the two prices must be of the same type. Recognize that if either condition is violated, the purchase is invalid (fasid).
The act is repurchasing an item previously sold, at a price less than the original sale price.
2
Understand the proof for the essence condition
The proof is a qiyas (analogy): a decline in market value is like a decline in desire, not a loss of a part of the item itself. The author cites the case of the usurper (ghasib) who returns an item after market drop — no compensation for the drop because it's not a real loss. Similarly, a seller cannot use market fluctuation to buy back cheaper.
The decrease must be physical — e.g., the item lost a part or developed a defect — to permit a lower buyback price.
3
Analyze the condition of same type of price
The two prices (original price and new price) must be of the same currency type (jins) for the decrease to be apparent. If they differ (e.g., original in dirhams, new in dinars), the purchase is absolutely permitted regardless of decrease. Dirhams and dinars are treated as one type here as a precaution, though generally considered two types except in eight cases.
This condition ensures that the decrease is measured in identical units; otherwise, no valid comparison.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a scenario, determine if the repurchase is valid or invalid by checking: (1) Is the decrease due to a physical change (loss of part, defect) or just market fluctuation? (2) Are the prices of the same type? If both conditions are met, the purchase is valid; if either fails, it is fasid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بد أن يكون النقصان فيها من حيث الذات لأن العين لو نقصت قيمتها بتغير الأسعار لم يجز الشراء بالأقل لأن تغيير السعر غير معتبر في حق الأحكام لأنه فتور في الرغبات لا فوات جزء كما في حق الغاصب وغيره فعاد إليه كما خرج عن ملكه فظهر الربح وقيد بالأقل احترازاً عن المثل أو الأكثر فإنه جائز، ولا بد من اتحاد جنس الثمنين لأنه حينئذ يظهر النقصان فإن اختلف الجنس جاز مطلقاً والدراهم والدنانير هنا جنس واحد احتياطاً، وقدمنا أنهما جنسان إلا في ثمانية في أول البيوع
It is necessary that the decrease in it be from the aspect of the essence, because if the 'ayn's value decreases due to a change in prices, it is not permitted to purchase it for less, because a change in price is not considered in the rulings because it is a decline in desire, not a loss of part, as with the usurper and others. So it returns to him as it left his ownership, and profit appears. He restricted it with 'less' as a precaution against equal or more, for that is permitted. It is also necessary that the two prices be of the same type, because then the decrease appears. If the type differs, it is absolutely permitted. Dirhams and dinars here are one type as a precaution, and we have presented that they are two types except in eight [cases] at the beginning of sales.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
The author continues by explaining that the decrease must be in the essence of the item (dhāt), not merely a fluctuation in market price. A market decline is not considered a true decrease because it is a change in desire, not a loss of a part. Therefore, buying back at a lower price due to market fall is invalid. Additionally, the two prices (the original price and the new price) must be of the same type of currency. If they differ, the purchase is permitted absolutely. Dirhams and dinars are treated as one type here for precaution, though they are two types generally except in eight cases mentioned earlier.

Key Terms
الذات (al-dhāt): The essence or physical substance of the item, as opposed to its market value.
جنس الثمنين (jins al-thamanayn): The type/class of the two prices; they must be the same currency type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The decrease must be due to market fluctuation
B) The decrease must be in the essence of the item
C) The decrease must be due to a defect only
D) The decrease must be equal to the reduction in price

Key Takeaway
A repurchase at a lower price is valid only if the decrease is in the item's essence and the prices are of the same type.

Buy-Back with an Additional Item, Oil Container Conditions, and Dispute on Container Weight
Ruling with proof, intra-Hanafi dispute, and procedural ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the spread of invalidity when buying back the sold item with an additional item, explain which condition for weighing oil with its container is valid, and determine whose word is accepted in a dispute about the container's weight.

Core Idea
Invalidity does not spread when weak; buyer's word on container weight; weighing condition valid if required by contract.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with several related sale (buyūʿ) issues: the effect of attaching an additional item to a buy-back sale, the condition of weighing oil with its container, and the dispute about the container's weight. It illustrates the Hanafi principle that weak invalidity (due to ijtihād) does not spread, and clarifies procedural rules for container disputes. The text also includes an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the spread of invalidity in certain salam contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling on buy-back with an additional item
Focus on the scenario where the seller buys back his sold item along with another item from the buyer for the same total price. Determine the validity of each part.
The sale is fasid for the original item but valid for the additional one.
2
Analyze why invalidity does not spread
Understand the three reasons given: invalidity is weak due to ijtihad, it is based on suspicion of riba, or it is incidental. The weakness prevents spreading.
The Ramli commentary reinforces that the invalidity is subject to ijtihad.
3
Examine the salam analogy and intra-Hanafi dispute
Study the salam examples (qūhī, marwī, harwī) to see how the Sahibayn differ on spread of invalidity when the invalidity is due to jinsiyya (type).
Abu Hanifa holds invalidity does not spread; Sahibayn analogize to cases where it does.
4
Apply the condition for weighing oil with its container
Distinguish between two conditions: subtracting a fixed weight (invalid) and subtracting the actual weight of the container (valid). The latter is required by the contract.
The first condition is not necessitated by the contract; the second is.
5
Determine the container weight dispute
If buyer and seller differ on the weight of the container (ziqq), the buyer's word is accepted with his oath. Understand the reasoning and the two objections raised.
The buyer denies any increase in price; thus his word prevails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وصح فيما ضم إليه) أي صح البيع في المضموم إلى شراء ما باعه بالأقل قبل النقد كأن اشترى جارية بخمسمائة ثم باعها وأخرى معها من البائع قبل أن ينقده الثمن بخمسمائه فالبيع جائز في التي لم يشترها من البائع ويفسد في الأخرى لأنه لا بد أن يجعل بعض الثمن في مقابلة التي لم يشترها منه فيكون مشترياً للأخرى بأقل مما باع وهذا فاسد عندنا، ولم يوجد هذا المعنى في صاحبتها ولا يشيع الفساد لكونه ضعيفاً للاجتهاد فيه أو لأنه باعتبار شبهة الربا أو لأنه طارئ لأنه يظهر بانقسام الثمن والمقاصة فلا يسري إلى غيرها . وأورد على التعليل الأول ما لو أسلم قوهياً في قوهي ومروي فإنه باطل في الكل عنده، يصح في المروي كما لو الفساد بالإجماع عليه إلا تعليله بأنه يجعل الشرط الفاسد في أحدهما وهو قبول العقد في الهروي شرطاً لقبوله في المروي فيفسد في المروي بالشرط الفاسد، وفي الهروي باتحاد الجنس؛ كذا اعترف به الأئمة بعد أن علل به هو في شرح الجامع. وأشار المصنف إلى أن البائع لو اشتراه مع رجل آخر فإنه يجوز من الأجنبي في نصفه قوله : وزيت على أن يزنه بظربه ويطرح عنه مكان كل ظرف خمسين رطلاً وصح لو شرط أن يطرح عنه بوزن الظرف) أي لم يجز بيع شيء بهذا الشرط وصح البيع بالشرط الثاني لأن الشرط الأول لا يقتضيه العقد والثاني بقتضيه قوله : (وإن اختلفا في الزق فالقول للمشتري) يعني لو رد المشتري الزق وهو عشرة أرطال فقال البائع الزق غيره وهو خمسة أرطال فالقول قول المشتري مع يمينه لأنه إن اعتبر اختلافاً في تعيين الزق المقبوض فالقول قول القابض ضميناً كان أو أميناً، وإن اعتبر اختلافاً في السمن فهو في الحقيقة اختلاف في الثمن فيكون القول للمشتري لأنه ينكر الزيادة، وإذا برهن البائع قبلت بينته. وأورد على ما في الكتاب مسألتان : إحداهما ما إذا باع عبدين وقبضهما المشتري ومات أحدهما عنده وجاء بالآخر يرده بعيب واختلفا في قيمة الميت فالقول للبائع. والثانية أن الاختلاف في الثمن يوجب التحالف وهنا جعل القول للمشتري على تقدير اختلافهما في الثمن. وأجيب عن الأول بأنها مع هذه طرد فإن كون القول للمشتري لإنكاره للزيادة وهناك إنما كان للبائع لإنكاره الزيادة وعن الثاني بأن التحالف على خلاف القياس فيها عند وجود الاختلاف في الثمن قصداً وهنا الاختلاف فيه تبع لاختلافهما في الزق المقبوض أهو هذا أم التحالف ؛ كذا يوجب في فتح القدير والزق بالكسر الظرف وبعضهم يقول ظرف زيت أو قبر والجمع أزقاق وزقاق وزقان مثل كتاب ورغفان؛ كذا في المصباح. لا فلا قوله : (ولا يشيع الفساد لكونه ضعيفاً للاجتهاد فيه قال الرملي أقول : ولم يـ يسر الفساد إلى الثانية لأنه ضعيف لكونه مجتهداً فيه أي محل اجتهاد وقابل له وإلا فخلاف الشافعي إنما جاء بعد وضع المسألة فكيف يوضع على شيء لم يقع بعد؟ ويجوز أن يكون الخلاف واقعاً قبل وضعها بل هو
His statement: 'And it is valid in what is attached to it' means the sale is valid for what is attached to the purchase of what he sold for less before payment. For example, if he bought a slave girl for five hundred, then sold her and another with her to the seller before paying him the price for five hundred, the sale is valid for the one he did not buy from the seller, and invalid for the other, because he must allocate part of the price for the one he did not buy from him, making him a buyer of the other for less than what he sold, and this is invalid according to us. This meaning is not found in the other, and the invalidity does not spread because it is weak due to ijtihad, or because it is based on suspicion of riba, or because it is incidental as it appears by division of price and set-off, so it does not spread to others. He objected to the first reasoning: if someone enters into a salam contract for qūhī against qūhī and marwī, it is invalid in all according to him, valid for the marwī as if he enters into salam for wheat in exchange for barley and oil, according to him it is invalid in all, but according to the two it is valid for the share of oil, even though the invalidity of the contract due to type is subject to ijtihad. If he enters into salam for harwī against harwī, it is valid according to al-Shafi'i, and there is no escape except by changing the reasoning for the spread of invalidity due to the strength of invalidity by consensus, except his reasoning that he makes the invalid condition in one of them, and accepting the contract in al-harwī is a condition for accepting it in al-marwī, so it becomes invalid in al-marwī due to the invalid condition, and in al-harwī due to unity of type. This is acknowledged by the imams after he reasoned with it in Sharh al-Jami'. The author indicated that if the seller buys it with another man, it is permissible from the stranger in half of it. His statement: 'and oil on condition that he weighs it with its container and subtracts from it the weight of each container fifty ratls, and it is valid if he stipulates to subtract the weight of the container' means: it is not permissible to sell anything with this condition, and the sale is valid with the second condition because the first condition is not required by the contract, and the second is required by it. His statement: 'and if they differ about the container, the word is that of the buyer' means: if the buyer returns the container and it is ten ratls, and the seller says the container is different and is five ratls, then the word is that of the buyer with his oath, because if considered a difference in identifying the container received, the word is that of the receiver, whether he is a guarantor or a trustee. If considered a difference in the oil, it is in reality a difference in the price, so the word is that of the buyer because he denies the increase. If the seller provides evidence, his evidence is accepted. Two objections are raised against what is in the book: first, if he sells two slaves and the buyer takes possession, one dies with him, and he returns the other due to a defect, and they differ on the value of the dead one, the word is that of the seller. Second, that difference about the price entails mutual oath, and here the word is given to the buyer on the assumption that they differ about the price. The first is answered: it is consistent, because the word is given to the buyer for his denial of increase, and there it was given to the seller for his denial of increase. The second is answered: mutual oath is against analogy when there is a direct difference about the price, but here the difference is subsidiary to their difference about the container received—is it this or that? This is required in Fath al-Qadir. Al-ziqq (with kasrah) is the container; some say it is a container for oil or wine; the plural is azqāq, ziqāq, and ziqān like kitāb and rughfān; this is in al-Misbah. Then his statement: 'and the invalidity does not spread because it is weak due to ijtihad'—al-Ramli said: I say: the invalidity does not spread to the second because it is weak due to being subject to ijtihad, i.e., it is a place of ijtihad and open to it; otherwise, the disagreement of al-Shafi'i only came after the formulation of the issue, so how can it be formulated on something that has not occurred? It is possible that the disagreement occurred before its formulation, rather it is...
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage covers several branches. First, if the seller buys back the sold item along with another item from the buyer for the same total price, the sale is valid for the additional item but invalid for the original item because part of the price is allocated to the additional item, making the purchase of the original at a lower price. The invalidity does not spread to the additional item because it is weak (due to ijtihād). Then the author discusses the case of selling oil with the condition of weighing it with its container and subtracting a fixed weight. This condition is invalid because it is not necessitated by the contract; however, if the condition is to subtract the actual weight of the container, it is valid. Finally, there is a dispute about the container (ziqq): if the buyer and seller differ on its weight, the word of the buyer (with his oath) is accepted because he denies the increase. Two objections are raised and answered, including a case of dead slave and mutual oath.

Key Terms
ضم (ḍamm): Attaching an additional item to the purchase back of the sold item.
الزق (al-ziqq): Container, especially for oil or wine; its weight is disputed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a seller buys back his sold item along with another item for the same total price, what is the ruling on the additional item?
A) It is invalid
B) It is valid
C) It is valid only if the buyer agrees
D) It is invalid because of the fasad

Key Takeaway
Invalidity from a fasid transaction does not spread to attached items if it is weak and based on ijtihad; the buyer's word on container weight is accepted; and a condition that is not necessitated by the contract invalidates the sale.
